### [1] [Detectability of post-Newtonian classical and quantum gravity via quantum clock interferometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15014)
*Eyuri Wakakuwa*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究利用双孔夫琅禾费衍射实验，通过测量光子在环绕中子星的光谱偏移，试图探测广义相对论效应对量子系统的干扰，但发现预期效果过小，无法在当前实验条件下检测。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 探索量子力学和广义相对论在极端条件下的相互作用，尤其是时空 dragging 效应对光谱的影响。

Method: 采用双孔夫琅禾费衍射实验，通过计算光子在环绕中子星的情况下产生的光谱偏移量，评估该效应的可见性。

Result: 计算表明，在实际实验条件下，光谱偏移过于微小而无法被探测，这限制了实验的可行性。

Conclusion: 该方案为未来探测时空 dragging 效应提供了理论框架，但需要更高灵敏度的探测器或更精确的实验参数来观察效应。此外，结果提示实验条件对广义相对论效应的探测能力有限，为量子引力研究提供了限制条件。

Abstract: Understanding physical phenomena at the intersection of quantum mechanics and
general relativity remains a major challenge in modern physics. While various
experimental approaches have been proposed to probe quantum systems in curved
spacetime, most focus on the Newtonian regime, leaving post-Newtonian effects
such as frame dragging largely unexplored. In this study, we propose and
theoretically analyze an experimental scheme to investigate how post-Newtonian
gravity affects quantum systems. We consider two setups: (i) a quantum clock
interferometry configuration designed to detect the gravitational field of a
rotating mass, and (ii) a scheme exploring whether such effects could mediate
entanglement between quantum systems. Due to the symmetry of the configuration,
the proposed setup is insensitive to Newtonian gravitational contributions but
remains sensitive to the frame-dragging effect. Assuming the validity of the
quantum equivalence principle, this approach may provide insights not only into
the quantum nature of gravity but also into whether spacetime itself exhibits
quantum properties. However, our analysis reveals that, within realistic
experimental parameters, the expected effects are too small to be detected. We
discuss possible interpretations of this undetectability, and its implications
for tests of quantum gravity.

</details>


### [2] [The logical structure of contextuality and nonclassicality](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15071)
*Songyi Liu,Yongjun Wang,Baoshan Wang,Chang He,Jinchng Wang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper explores quantum contextuality and its relation to nonclassicality by developing a logic algebra framework. It shows contextuality is a sufficient but not necessary condition for nonclassicality, identifies quantum experiments that exhibit nonclassicality without contextuality, and suggests simpler measurement configurations for detecting contextuality.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper is motivated by the debate around the role of contextuality in quantum mechanics and its connection to nonclassicality. It aims to provide a clearer understanding by developing a new framework and demonstrating its practical applications.

Method: The method involves creating a mathematical framework using logic algebra to compare classical and quantum experiments, characterizing contextuality and nonclassicality, and analyzing specific examples to showcase the findings.

Result: The key results include proving contextuality is a sufficient but not necessary condition for nonclassicality, identifying quantum experiments that demonstrate nonclassicality without contextuality, and highlighting the potential for simplified measurements using 3 projectors and 3 measurements.

Conclusion: The paper concludes that while contextuality plays a significant role, it is not the sole determinant of nonclassicality, and simpler measurement setups can be used to detect contextuality, offering a promising approach for quantum studies.

Abstract: Quantum contextuality is known as the fundamental feature of quantum
mechanics. It is not clear whether contextuality fully reveals the nonclassical
aspects of quantum mechanics. To answer this question, we propose a
mathematical framework based on logic algebra to compare classical and quantum
experiments. With the framework, we precisely characterize the contextuality
and nonclassicality, reveal that the former is a sufficient but not necessary
condition for the latter, and present a type of quantum experiments which
exhibit nonclassicality without contextuality. We also point out that the
property of quantum systems is captured by the projector generators. Therefore,
it is possible to witness quantum contextuality with simplified measurement
configurations. For example, we show that 12 projectors witness the
Kochen-Specker contextuality, and 3 measurements are sufficient to witness the
quantum contextuality, as compared to the 4 presented in the compatibility
graph approach.

</details>


### [3] [Improving Quantum Battery Capacity in Tripartite Quantum Systems by Local Projective Measurements](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15074)
*Yiding Wang,Hui Liu,Shao-Ming Fei,Tinggui Zhang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该论文研究了局部冯·诺依曼测量对三部分量子系统电池容量的影响，提出了两种基于测量的协议，并引入了最优局部投影算子的概念。明确了对于一般三qubit X态，可以导出两种协议的显式解析表达式。此外，分析了白噪声和相干色噪声对电池容量的负面影响，并证明了最优局部投影算子可以提高子系统和整体系统的电池容量的抗噪声能力。通过数值例子验证了不同方案在提升电池容量方面的效果，结果显示局部冯·诺依曼测量是一个有效的工具以提高多部分量子系统的电池容量。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该论文研究的是量子系统的全局性问题，特别是量子电池容量的提升，这对于量子信息科学和量子计算都有重要的意义。研究者希望通过优化测量方法，提高量子系统在噪声干扰下的稳定性与实用性。

Method: 论文采用量子力学分析和数值模拟的方法，首先在三部分X态系统中提出了两种基于测量的协议，并通过数学推导得到了显式解析式。然后分析了噪声对电池容量的影响，并通过具体数学模型证明了最优的局部投影算子能够有效提升系统的抗噪声能力。最后通过数值例子验证了理论分析的有效性和方法的可行性。

Result: 论文得出的结果表明，局部冯·诺依曼测量是一个有效的工具，可以显著提高量子电池容量，特别是对三部分X态系统的整体性和子系统的寿命也非常有利。此外，通过分析不同噪声类型的影响，展示了该方法在抗噪声场景中的优势。

Conclusion: 该论文通过理论分析和数值验证，展示了局部冯·诺依曼测量在提升三部分量子系统电池容量方面的有效性。结果表明，最优的局部投影操作能够有效改善系统的抗噪声能力，为开发更实用和更稳定的量子电池提供了重要依据。

Abstract: The impact of local von Neumann measurements on quantum battery capacity is
investigated in tripartite quantum systems. Two measurement-based protocols are
proposed and the concept of optimal local projective operators is introduced.
Specifically, explicit analytical expressions are derived for the protocols
when applied to general three-qubit X-states. Furthermore, the negative effects
of white noise and dephasing noise on quantum battery capacity are analyzed,
proving that optimal local projective operators can improve the robustness of
subsystem and total system capacity against both noise types for the general
tripartite X-state. The performance of different schemes in capacity
enhancement are numerically validated through detailed examples and it is found
that these optimized operators can effectively enhance both subsystem and total
system battery capacity. The results indicate that the local von Neumann
measurement is a powerful tool to enhance the battery capacity in multipartite
quantum systems.

</details>


### [4] [Excitation Amplitude Sampling for Low Variance Electronic Structure on Quantum Computers](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15438)
*Connor Lenihan,Oliver J. Backhouse,Tom W. A. Montgomery,Phalgun Lolur,M. J. Bhaseen,George H. Booth*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究结合经典启发式和部分影射相位断层，提出新的能量估算方法和高效算法，显著提高估计准确性和系统的扩展性。研究结果表明，该方法在噪声较大的量子设备上表现出更高的抗噪能力，且在实际材料科学中得以应用，特别是在NiO晶体中的自旋间隙体积依赖性得到了验证。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 开发高效算法和精确方法用于量子计算中的能量估算，尤其是在需要处理高度相关和大规模量子系统时，提高计算效率和估算精度是关键。

Method: 采用经典启发式与部分影射相位断层结合，提出的能量估算方法和高效算法，包括使用相关能量泛函和采样多项式集合的激发振幅。

Result: 在能量估算中，该方法显著减少了所需采样次数，估计误差显著降低，观察到算法在系统大小上的线性可扩展性。在量子设备的高噪声情况下，该方法表现出显著更高的抗噪能力。

Conclusion: 该方法为在量子计算器中处理大范围相关电子系统提供了高效的解决方案，并在实际材料科学中得到了验证，展示了显著的优势。

Abstract: We combine classical heuristics with partial shadow tomography to enable
efficient protocols for extracting information from correlated ab initio
electronic systems encoded on quantum devices. By proposing the use of a
correlation energy functional and sampling of a polynomial set of excitation
amplitudes of the quantum state, we can demonstrate an almost two order of
magnitude reduction in required number of shots for a given statistical error
in the energy estimate, as well as observing a linear scaling to accessible
system sizes. Furthermore, we find a high-degree of noise resilience of these
estimators on real quantum devices, with up to an order of magnitude increase
in the tolerated noise compared to traditional techniques. While these
approaches are expected to break down asymptotically, we find strong evidence
that these large system arguments do not prevent algorithmic advantage from
these simple protocols in many systems of interest. We further extend this to
consider the extraction of beyond-energetic properties by mapping to a coupled
cluster surrogate model, as well as a natural combination within a quantum
embedding framework. This embedding framework avoids the unstable
self-consistent requirements of previous approaches, enabling application of
quantum solvers to realistic correlated materials science, where we demonstrate
the volume-dependence of the spin gap of Nickel Oxide.

</details>


### [5] [Notes on detection and measurement of quantum coherence](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15080)
*Yiding Wang,Tinggui Zhang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper proposes methods to detect and measure quantum coherence. It introduces a coherence criterion using partial transposition without full quantum state tomography. A nonlinear detection strategy using witnesses is presented, which works for some states where standard detection fails. The paper also shows that increasing the number of copies can sometimes enhance detection. Lower bounds for coherence are discussed, with the new bound being more effective. The results have implications for quantum information tasks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper contributes to detecting quantum coherence, a key aspect of quantum mechanics with applications in quantum information processing. The methods presented could improve the experimental detection of quantum states and quantum communication protocols.

Method: The paper utilizes partial transposition criteria and nonlinear witnesses for detection. It involves theoretical analysis, numerical calculations, and comparisons with existing methods.

Result: Coherent states can sometimes evade standard detection, but nonlinear methods can succeed, and increasing copies may help. Lower bounds for coherence availability are developed with improved performance.

Conclusion: The study advances detection methods, enhancing the ability to measure quantum coherence, which is essential for quantum computing and information theory.

Abstract: Quantum coherence is one of the most basic characteristics of quantum
mechanics. Here we give some methods to detect and measure quantum coherence.
Firstly, we propose a coherence criterion without full quantum state tomography
based on partial transposition. Moreover, we present a coherent nonlinear
detection strategy from witnesses, in which we find that for some coherent
states, normal witness detection fails but our nonlinear detection succeeds. In
addition, we prove that when the nonlinear detection on the two copies of the
coherent state fails, the nonlinear detection on the three copies may be
successful. Finally, due to the difficulty in calculating robustness of
coherence for general states, we introduce a lower bound for coherent
robustness based on the witness operator, and after comparing our lower bound
with the currently known lower bound, one show that our lower bound is better.
Coherence is believed to play a crucial role in quantum information tasks,
making the detection and quantization of coherence particularly significant.
Therefore, these results help to open up new avenues for advancement in quantum
theory.

</details>


### [6] [Aperiodic Dissipation as a Mechanism for Steady-State Localization](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15108)
*Shilpi Roy,Jiangbin Gong*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究发现不规则消散能够诱导稳态局域化，消散参数的长程 phases促进了相干效应，消散作为主动因素参与了局域化。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究者试图理解开放量子系统中的局域化机制，特别是如何通过引入不规则的消散来实现。

Method: 研究者通过引入两个不同类型的不规则消散（有理与无理情况）进行数值模拟，计算相干性和局域性的度量。

Result: 发现无理模的消散更有效，消散参数的长程相关性促进了局域状态。

Conclusion: 可以利用非周期消散来控制局域化，这提供了新途径来操控量子态和设计消散驱动态。

Abstract: Dissipation is traditionally regarded as a disruptive factor in quantum
systems because it often leads to decoherence and delocalization. However,
recent insights into engineered dissipation reveal that it can be tuned to
facilitate various quantum effects, from state stabilization to phase
transitions. In this work, we identify aperiodic dissipation as a mechanism for
inducing steady-state localization, independent of disorder or a quasiperiodic
potential in the Hamiltonian. This localization arises from long-range phase
correlations introduced by a spatially varying dissipation phase parameter,
which enables nontrivial interference in the steady-state. By systematically
comparing two classes of aperiodic dissipation (defined as commensurate and
incommensurate cases), we find that incommensurate modulation plays the most
efficient role in stabilizing a localized steady-state. Our analysis, based on
coherence measures, purity, and participation ratio, reveals a direct link
between eigenstate coherence and real-space localization, showing that
dissipation can actively shape localization rather than simply causing
decoherence. These findings highlight aperiodic dissipation as a viable
approach to controlling localization in open quantum systems, potentially
enabling new ways to manipulate quantum states and design dissipation-driven
phases.

</details>


### [7] [Optimal Compilation Strategies for QFT Circuits in Neutral-Atom Quantum Computing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15116)
*Dingchao Gao,Yongming Li,Shenggang Ying,Sanjiang Li*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 这篇论文讨论了中性原子量子计算（NAQC）的优势，并提出了优化的编译策略来提高量子傅里叶变换（QFT）的效率。通过减少原子移动次数，他们的方法达到了理论下限，且保持了高电路 fidelity。与现有的编译器相比，他们的方法表现更好。初步结论是他们的方法是NAQC编译器的基准。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 中性原子量子计算作为量子计算的平台，在动态重配置、长相干时间和高门限方面有显著优势，但如何高效地编译量子电路如QFT仍是一个挑战。因此，研究如何优化编译策略来提高效率和门限是非常有必要的。

Method: 论文提出了一种优化的编译策略，针对线性和网格型架构，通过减少原子移动次数来解决QFT电路的原子运动和连接性瓶颈。使用理论下限和高电路 fidelity作为评估指标。

Result: 通过与现有编译器的比较，他们的方法在减少原子移动次数和保持高 fidelity方面表现更好，特别是在理论下限上。

Conclusion: 研究为NAQC平台上的QFT电路优化提供了新的方法，可作为未来编译器的基准。

Abstract: Neutral-atom quantum computing (NAQC) offers distinct advantages such as
dynamic qubit reconfigurability, long coherence times, and high gate
fidelities, making it a promising platform for scalable quantum computing.
Despite these strengths, efficiently implementing quantum circuits like the
Quantum Fourier Transform (QFT) remains a significant challenge due to atom
movement overheads and connectivity constraints. This paper introduces optimal
compilation strategies tailored to QFT circuits and NAQC systems, addressing
these challenges for both linear and grid-like architectures. By minimizing
atom movements, the proposed methods achieve theoretical lower bounds in atom
movements while preserving high circuit fidelity. Comparative evaluations
against state-of-the-art compilers demonstrate the superior performance of the
proposed methods. These methods could serve as benchmarks for evaluating the
performance of NAQC compilers.

</details>


### [8] [A Topologically Fault-Tolerant Quantum Computer with Four Dimensional Geometric Codes](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15130)
*David Aasen,Matthew B. Hastings,Vadym Kliuchnikov,Juan M. Bello-Rivas,Adam Paetznick,Rui Chao,Ben W. Reichardt,Matt Zanner,Marcus P. da Silva,Zhenghan Wang,Krysta M. Svore*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Topological quantum codes have shown potential for fault-tolerant quantum computing. The paper introduces a 4D code with improved parameters and a universal fault-tolerant architecture. The code achieves single-shot error correction and efficient syndrome extraction. The proposed design is applicable for near-term quantum hardware.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The development of topological quantum codes is significant because they provide inherent fault tolerance, which is crucial for the scalability of quantum computing. This paper aims to further enhance their performance by leveraging higher-dimensional structures and optimizing both qubit count and error correction capabilities.

Method: The authors introduce a 4-dimensional topological quantum code, specifically a [[96,6,8]] code, with low-weight stabilizers and efficient syndrome extraction circuits. They also present a full set of logical Clifford operations and a universal fault-tolerant architecture. The method involves constructing low-depth logical circuits and employing adaptive syndrome extraction methods.

Result: The code achieves single-shot error correction, reducing the number of required qubits while maintaining low logical error rates. The depth-8 syndrome extraction and low stabilizer weights contribute to effective error correction. The logical error rate is around 10^-6 at a physical error rate of 10^-3, and the code supports a Clstone-based universal fault-tolerant structure.

Conclusion: The proposed architecture advances the practicality of topological quantum codes, especially for near-term quantum devices, by optimizing resource usage and fault tolerance. This work paves the way for leveraging higher-dimensional topological codes in quantum computing systems.

Abstract: Topological quantum codes are intrinsically fault-tolerant to local noise,
and underlie the theory of topological phases of matter. We explore geometry to
enhance the performance of topological quantum codes by rotating the four
dimensional self-correcting quantum memory, and present codes targeted to both
near-term and utility-scale quantum computers. We identify a full set of
logical Clifford operations and with it design a universal fault-tolerant
quantum architecture. Our design achieves single-shot error correction,
significant reductions in required qubits, and low-depth logical operations. In
turn, our proposed architecture relaxes the requirements for achieving fault
tolerance and offers an efficient path for realization in several near-term
quantum hardware implementations. Our [[96,6,8]] 4D Hadamard lattice code has
low weight-6 stabilizers and depth-8 syndrome extraction circuits, a high
pseudo-threshold of $\sim 0.01$, and a logical error rate of $\sim 10^{-6}$ per
logical qubit per round of error correction at $10^{-3}$ physical error rate
under a standard circuit-level noise model. A Clifford-complete logical gate
set is presented, including a constructive and efficient method for Clifford
gate synthesis.

</details>


### [9] [Time-bin encoded quantum key distribution over 120 km with a telecom quantum dot source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15520)
*Jipeng Wang,Joscha Hanel,Zenghui Jiang,Raphael Joos,Michael Jetter,Eddy Patrick Rugeramigabo,Simone Luca Portalupi,Peter Michler,Xiao-Yu Cao,Hua-Lei Yin,Shan Lei,Jingzhong Yang,Michael Zopf,Fei Ding*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 这项研究利用量子点光源实现了光子时间编码量子密钥分发系统，成功在120公里光纤上传输并保持了持续6小时的稳定，显示出高安全性和有效的密钥速率。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着量子通信技术的发展，提高密钥分发的安全性和可靠性是关键，特别是在大规模实测中的应用。

Method: 采用了高亮度量子点光源作为单光子源，结合时间编码，通过实验验证了在长距离光纤上传输及长期稳定的KM.研究得到了更高的密钥速率和更长的通信距离。

Result: 首次实现了基于量子点单光子源的时间编码量子密钥分发，成功在120公里光纤上传输并保持6小时稳定，密钥速率最高。

Conclusion: 这项研究展示了基于量子点技术的光子时间编码在实现可靠量子密钥分发方面的巨大进步，为构建实用的量子通信网络奠定了基础。这种技术不仅适用于现有光纤网络，还能扩展到自由空间。

Abstract: Quantum key distribution (QKD) with deterministic single photon sources has
been demonstrated over intercity fiber and free-space channels. The previous
implementations relied mainly on polarization encoding schemes, which are
susceptible to birefringence, polarization-mode dispersion and
polarization-dependent loss in practical fiber networks. In contrast, time-bin
encoding offers inherent robustness and has been widely adopted in mature QKD
systems using weak coherent laser pulses. However, its feasibility in
conjunction with a deterministic single-photon source has not yet been
experimentally demonstrated. In this work, we construct a time-bin encoded QKD
system employing a high-brightness quantum dot (QD) single-photon source
operating at telecom wavelength. Our proof-of-concept experiment successfully
demonstrates the possibility of secure key distribution over fiber link of 120
km, while maintaining extraordinary long-term stability over 6 hours of
continuous operation. This work provides the first experimental validation of
integrating a quantum dot single-photon source with time-bin encoding in a
telecom-band QKD system. In addition, it demonstrates the highest secure key
rate among the time-bin QKDs based on single-photon sources. This development
signifies a substantial advancement in the establishment of a robust and
scalable QKD network based on solid-state single-photon technology

</details>


### [10] [Catalytic $z$-rotations in constant $T$-depth](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15147)
*Isaac H. Kim*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究显示，利用特定的催化剂态，可以将单比特Z旋转的T深度降低到3，在一定精度下催化剂的尺寸与对数(1/精度)成多项式关系。这表明有限门集的量子非可计算类允许任意精度的多比特门电路。催化剂态可以在多项式时间内准备。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 本研究关注如何降低量子计算中T门的深度，T深度对量子电路的深度敏感，降低T深度有助于优化量子电路性能。

Method: 研究使用了催化剂态，通过将单比特门分解为多个三深度操作，再利用催化剂态提升整体深度。

Result: 结果证明催化剂态的存在可以有效降低T深度，并且可以在合理时间准备这样的催化剂态。

Conclusion: 研究结论显示有限门集可以实现多比特任意精度门，这对于量子计算的重要应用有帮助。

Abstract: We show that the $T$-depth of any single-qubit $z$-rotation can be reduced to
$3$ if a certain catalyst state is available. To achieve an
$\epsilon$-approximation, it suffices to have a catalyst state of size
polynomial in $\log(1/\epsilon)$. This implies that
$\mathsf{QNC}^0_f/\mathsf{qpoly}$ admits a finite universal gate set consisting
of Clifford+$T$. In particular, there are catalytic constant $T$-depth circuits
that approximate multi-qubit Toffoli, adder, and quantum Fourier transform
arbitrarily well. We also show that the catalyst state can be prepared in time
polynomial in $\log (1/\epsilon)$.

</details>


### [11] [Entangling remote superconducting qubits via transducer-generated multi-time-bin states](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15277)
*Jing Wu,Changqing Wang,Andrew Cameron,Silvia Zorzetti*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Recent studies using NV centers and quantum dots show entanglement over long distances. We propose a method to entangle remote superconducting qubits using microwave-optical transduction with multi-time-bin states. The method improves entanglement fidelity by up to 33% in clean systems and 36% in noisy systems compared to standard swapping techniques. It also addresses thermal noise without purification, offering a good path for scalable quantum systems.

Method: The method uses microwave-optical transduction with multi-time-bin states to mediate entanglement between superconducting qubits. It improves upon traditional entanglement swapping by enhancing fidelity and mitigating noise.

Result: The protocol achieves a 0.75 to 0.98 fidelity improvement in transduction systems and 0.66 to 0.89 in noisy channels.

Conclusion: The proposed method offers a practical solution to long-distance entanglement, addresses thermal noise, and reduces reliance on purification, making it a promising step toward scalable quantum systems.

Abstract: Recent studies have shown long-distance entanglement using NV centers, atoms,
and quantum dots with single-photon time-bin encoding. We propose a method to
entangle remote superconducting qubits via microwave-optical transduction using
multi-time-bin states. By adapting conventional entanglement swapping
techniques, fidelity improves from 0.75 to $0.98$ in transduction systems, and

Abstract: Whether gravity must be quantized remains one of the biggest open problems in
fundamental physics. Classical-quantum hybrid theories have recently attracted
attention as a possible framework in which gravity is treated classically yet
interacts consistently with quantum matter. Schemes based on completely
positive dynamics satisfy most formal consistency requirements and enable a
systematic treatment of quantum backreaction, but they also give rise to
features that challenge conventional physical intuition, such as the breakdown

with a classical particle and demonstrate that the corresponding hybrid system

Abstract: Quantum multiparameter estimation aims to simultaneously estimate multiple

two-parameter estimation precision. We also develop an error ellipse method to

the phase-space complex displacement estimation. Our research shows that
multiparameter estimation challenges can be effectively addressed by
manipulating the geometry of multidimensional parameter space.

Abstract: Equilibrium and nonequilibrium states of matter can exhibit fundamentally
different behavior. A key example is the Kardar-Parisi-Zhang universality class
in two spatial dimensions (2D KPZ), where microscopic deviations from

counterparts. While extensively studied theoretically, direct experimental

exploring 2D nonequilibrium universality quantitatively, and open new avenues
for investigating the emergence of coherence in interacting quantum systems far
from equilibrium.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Abstract: Quantum neural networks (QNNs) are widely employed as ans\"atze for solving
variational problems, where their expressivity directly impacts performance.
Yet, accurately characterizing QNN expressivity remains an open challenge,
impeding the optimal design of quantum circuits. In this work, we introduce the
effective rank, denoted as $\kappa$, as a novel quantitative measure of
expressivity. Specifically, $\kappa$ captures the number of effectively
independent parameters among all the variational parameters in a parameterized
quantum circuit, thus reflecting the true degrees of freedom contributing to
expressivity. Through a systematic analysis considering circuit architecture,
input data distributions, and measurement protocols, we demonstrate that
$\kappa$ can saturate its theoretical upper bound, $d_n=4^n-1$, for an
$n$-qubit system when each of the three factors is optimally expressive. This
result provides a rigorous framework for assessing QNN expressivity and
quantifying their functional capacity. Building on these theoretical insights,
and motivated by the vast and highly structured nature of the circuit design
space, we employ $\kappa$ as a guiding metric for the automated design of
highly expressive quantum circuit configurations. To this end, we develop a
reinforcement learning framework featuring a self-attention transformer agent
that autonomously explores and optimizes circuit architectures. By integrating
theoretical characterization with practical optimization, our work establishes
$\kappa$ as a robust tool for quantifying QNN expressivity and demonstrates the
effectiveness of reinforcement learning in designing high-performance quantum
circuits. This study paves the way for building more expressive QNN
architectures, ultimately enhancing the capabilities of quantum machine
learning.

Abstract: Dynamical decoupling (DD) is a well-known open-loop protocol for suppressing
unwanted interactions in a quantum system, thereby drastically extending the
coherence time of useful quantum states. In the original framework of evolution
symmetrization, a DD sequence was shown to enforce a symmetry on the unwanted
Hamiltonian, thereby suppressing it if the symmetry was inaccessible. In this
work, we show how symmetries already present in the undesired Hamiltonian can
be harnessed to reduce the complexity of decoupling sequences and to construct
nested protocols that correct dominant errors at shorter timescales, using the
factorization of DD symmetry groups into a product of its subgroups. We provide
many relevant examples in various spin systems, using the Majorana
constellation and point-group factorization to identify and exploit symmetries
in the interaction Hamiltonian. Our framework recovers tailored pulse sequences
developed in the context of NMR and further produces novel short and robust
sequences capable of suppressing on-site disorder, dipole-dipole interactions,
and more exotic many-body interactions in spin ensembles.

Abstract: Amplitude damping is a dominant source of error in high performance quantum
processors. A promising approach in quantum error correction is erasure error

amplitude-damping errors; with unique sensitivities to noise and decoherence
sources. Here we present a dual-rail encoding within a single fixed-frequency
superconducting multimode transmon qubit. The three island, two junction device
comprises two transmonlike modes with a detuning of 0.75-1 GHz, in a coaxial

rates are more than one order of magnitude lower than the physical error rates,

extended measurement of three such devices. Finally, we discuss how the
error-detected subspace can be used for investigations into the fundamentals of

### [22] [Adaptive random compiler for Hamiltonian simulation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15466)
*Yun-Zhuo Fan,Yu-Xia Wu,Dan-Bo Zhang*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Randomized compilation protocols are a new approach for quantum circuit synthesis, reducing circuit depth and resource overhead by randomizing gate applications compared to traditional methods. They use the trace norm to measure Hamiltonian strengths but have limitations in certain systems. This paper proposes an adaptive algorithm that dynamically adjusts sampling probabilities based on moment measurements, improving accuracy in systems with unbounded operators like continuous-variable and hybrid-variable systems. Simulations show the method works well.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The traditional methods for quantum circuit synthesis, such as the Trotter-Suzuki method, are deterministic and can become resource-intensive for large circuits. The growing demand for efficient quantum computing, especially with more qubits and complex operations, necessitates new, more efficient methods. Randomized compilation protocols offer a promising alternative by introducing stochastic elements to reduce overhead. Additionally, the increasing complexity of quantum systems, particularly those involving unbounded operators, poses challenges for existing methods, making an adaptive approach more advantageous.

Method: The paper introduces an adaptive randomized compilation algorithm that dynamically updates the probabilities of applying quantum gates. This is achieved by measuring low-order moments of the Hamiltonian terms. The moments provide additional information beyond the trace norm, allowing the algorithm to better account for the uncertainty and strength of each term. By assigning higher probabilities to terms with greater uncertainty, the method aims to improve the overall accuracy of the compilation process.

Result: Numerical simulations conducted in the study demonstrate the effectiveness of the proposed adaptive algorithm. The results show improved accuracy in synthesizing quantum circuits, especially in systems where the Hamiltonian terms are unbounded, such as continuous-variable systems. The adaptive method requires similar or fewer gate counts compared to traditional deterministic methods, indicating a more efficient resource utilization.

Conclusion: The adaptive randomized compilation algorithm represents a significant advancement in quantum circuit synthesis. By dynamically adjusting gate application probabilities based on measured moments of Hamiltonian terms, the method addresses the limitations of static approaches and enhances the scalability and efficiency of quantum computing systems. This approach is particularly valuable for emerging quantum systems with complex Hamiltonians, offering a flexible and effective solution for future quantum algorithm development.

Abstract: Randomized compilation protocols have recently attracted attention as
alternatives to traditional deterministic Trotter-Suzuki methods, potentially
reducing circuit depth and resource overhead. These protocols determine gate
application probabilities based on the strengths of Hamiltonian terms, as
measured by the trace norm. However, relying solely on the trace norm to define
sampling distributions may not be optimal, especially for continuous-variable
and hybrid-variable systems involving unbounded operators, where quantifying
Hamiltonian strengths is challenging. In this work, we propose an adaptive
randomized compilation algorithm that dynamically updates sampling weights via
low-order moment measurements of Hamiltonian terms, assigning higher
probabilities to terms with greater uncertainty. This approach improves
accuracy without significantly increasing gate counts and extends randomized
compilation to continuous-variable and hybrid-variable systems by addressing
the difficulties in characterizing the strengths of unbounded Hamiltonian
terms. Numerical simulations demonstrate the effectiveness of our method.

physical system has non-classical features. Here we connect recently proposed
witnesses of non-classicality, based on information-theoretic ideas, with the
theory of temporal entanglement. We provide a protocol to witness the
non-classicality of a system by probing it with a qubit: we show that, assuming
a general conservation law, violating temporal Bell inequalities on the qubit
probe implies the non-classicality of the system under investigation. We also
perform proof-of-principle experimental emulations of the proposed witness of
non-classicality, using a three qubit Nuclear Magnetic Resonance quantum
computer. Our result is robust, as it relies on minimal assumptions, and
remarkably it can be applied in a broad range of contexts, from quantum biology
to quantum gravity.

</details>

Result: 结果显示，在弱相互作用下，双 qubit 门的时间比在强相互作用情况下短。同时，使用几何控制可以更有效地实现高效且鲁棒的门操作。

Abstract: In this manuscript we discuss the relationship between the gate time of
Rydberg two-qubit gate and the Rydberg interaction strength. Different from the
two-qbuit gates that directly depend on the interactions between the spins (or
pseudo spins), the ones in atomic arrays are realized by driving the atoms to
the Rydberg states. As a consequence, competition happens between shortening
the gate time and decreasing the excitation probability of Rydberg states. For
the case of Rydberg blockade, it is found that the gate time is irrelevant of
the Rydberg interaction strength. In contrast, for the case of weak Rydberg
interactions, the interactions will help to accelerate the two-qubit gates.
This implies that the scheme of weak Rydberg interactions will be faster than
the Rydberg blockade one to realize the two-qbuit gates under the same Rabi
frequencies of Rydberg excitation. Through using the geometric control under
the region of weak Rydberg interaction, fast and robust two-qubit gates can be
achieved in atomic arrays, of which detailed discussion can be referred to the
manuscript \textsl{arXiv:2412. 19193 (2024)}.

Abstract: Surface codes are promising for practical quantum error correction due to
their high threshold and experimental feasibility. However, their performance

symmetry, resulting in higher thresholds compared to other types of correlated
errors. This deepens our insight into the threshold of surface code and hence
facilitates a more robust design of quantum circuits with a higher noise

### [26] [${\sf QMA}={\sf QMA}_1$ with an infinite counter](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15551)
*Stacey Jeffery,Freek Witteveen*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper establishes that QMA equals QMA with an infinite verifier's infinite register and one-sided error variant, implying that such registers do not boost QMA's power but ensure perfect completeness. A new QMA-amplifier is introduced that significantly improves the time for amplifying completeness without affecting soundness.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: This paper addresses a fundamental question in quantum complexity theory regarding the equality of QMA and its one-sided error variant, QMA1. Demonstrating that QMA is equivalent to these variants with powerful insight into the role of infinite registers in quantum proofs.

Method: The authors introduce an infinite counter within QMA's framework, providing a novel verifier mechanism that allows for efficient increment operations on this counter. Leveraging a modular approach with a probabilistic algorithm, they construct a QMA-amplifier that improves both the speed of completeness amplification and reduces the number of required operations.

Result: The primary results show that QMA does not gain additional computational power from infinite registers or amplification, yet it achieves perfect completeness. The QMA-amplifier technology significantly enhances this improvement by enabling a more efficient process, achieving completion (1 - 2^{-2^{r}}) with fewer resources compared to previous methods.

Conclusion: This breakthrough clarifies the capabilities and limitations of QMA variants, demonstrating that infinite registers do not augment proof power, thus setting a new benchmark in quantum complexity theory and opening avenues for future research on QMA-related protocols.

Abstract: A long-standing open problem in quantum complexity theory is whether ${\sf
QMA}$, the quantum analogue of ${\sf NP}$, is equal to ${\sf QMA}_1$, its
one-sided error variant. We show that ${\sf QMA}={\sf QMA}^{\infty}= {\sf
QMA}_1^{\infty}$, where ${\sf QMA}_1^\infty$ is like ${\sf QMA}_1$, but the
verifier has an infinite register, as part of their witness system, in which
they can efficiently perform a shift (increment) operation. We call this
register an ``infinite counter'', and compare it to a program counter in a Las
Vegas algorithm. The result ${\sf QMA}={\sf QMA}^\infty$ means such an infinite
register does not increase the power of ${\sf QMA}$, but does imply perfect
completeness.
  By truncating our construction to finite dimensions, we get a ${\sf
QMA}$-amplifier that only amplifies completeness, not soundness, but does so in
significantly less time than previous ${\sf QMA}$ amplifiers. Our new
construction achieves completeness $1-2^{-q}$ using $O(1)$ calls to each of the
original verifier and its inverse, and $O(\log q)$ other gates, proving that
${\sf QMA}$ has completeness doubly exponentially close to 1, i.e. ${\sf
QMA}={\sf QMA}(1-2^{-2^r},2^{-r})$ for any polynomial $r$.

</details>


### [27] [Chiral Symmetries and Multiparticle Entanglement](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15609)
*Sophia Denker,Satoya Imai,Otfried Gühne*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: This paper discusses how chiral symmetries in multiparticle systems lead to extreme quantum entanglement, develop methods for analyzing genuine multipartite entanglement, and suggests potential applications.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding quantum entanglement is crucial for quantum computing and information theory. This paper contributes by linking chiral symmetries to high entanglement and providing new analysis methods.

Method: The paper introduces a method to solve multiparticle entanglement problems for unitarily invariant states and identifies states with positive partial transposes.

Result: Chiral symmetries cause high levels of entanglement and the identified states are useful for entanglement characterization.

Conclusion: Chiral symmetries yield maximally entangled states in multiparticle systems, which are valuable for entanglement detection, while generalizations may have applications in quantum information processing.

Abstract: Bosons and fermions are defined by their exchange properties and the
underlying symmetries determine the structure of the corresponding state
spaces. For two particles there are two possible exchange symmetries, resulting
in symmetric or antisymmetric behaviour, but when exploring multiparticle
systems also quantum states with chiral symmetries appear. In this work we
demonstrate that chiral symmetries lead to extremal forms of quantum
entanglement. More precisely, we show that subspaces with this symmetry are
highly entangled with respect to the geometric measure of entanglement, leading
to observables which can be useful for entanglement characterization. Along the
way, we develop a simple method to solve the problem of genuine multiparticle
entanglement for unitarily invariant three-particle states and use it to
identify genuine multipartite entangled states whose partial transposes with
respect to all bipartitions are positive. Finally, we consider generalizations
with less symmetry and discuss potential applications.

### [28] [Fast, continuous and coherent atom replacement in a neutral atom qubit array](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15633)
*Yiyi Li,Yicheng Bao,Michael Peper,Chenyuan Li,Jeff D. Thompson*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该论文提出了一种基于中性原子量子处理器的快速原子替代方法，通过利用 metastable $^{171}$Yb qubit 的孤立性，可以在 500 次/秒的频率下进行原子提取，并且可以在计算区附近建立新的 qubit 数组，频率高达 30 次/秒。这种快速替代方法显著减少了原子丢失造成的错误，并且不会干扰现有 qubit 的运行。这种方法为实现任意深度的量子电路奠定了基础，有助于下一步的纠错量子计算。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 实现大规模量子计算需要克服中性原子量子处理器中的原子丢失问题。当前的方法在实施长时间的量子电路时效率很低，甚至需要数倍于量子门和测量操作的时间来完成原子的替代。因此，开发一种高效、快速的原子替代方法是非常紧迫的研究课题。

Method: 论文通过使用靠近计算区的快换原子池，结合微针 tweezers 连续提取原子，并在 500 次/秒的频率下完成替换。同时，使用 metastable $^{171}$Yb qubit 作为量子位，确保替代过程中不会干扰现有 qubit 的运行。这种方法结合了高频率和低干扰的特点，能够实现快速的原子替代。此外，new qubit arrays 可以以30 次/秒的频率被准备起来，包括单个原子准备、非破坏性成像和初始化。

Result: 该方法显著提高了量子电路的深度，减少了原子丢失带来的错误率。能够在 500 次/秒的替代频率下实现量子操作，同时不干扰现有 qubit 的运行。实验结果证实了这种方法的有效性，为实现长深度的量子电路提供了关键的技术基础。

Conclusion: 该研究成功开发了一种快速、高效且低干扰的原子替代方法，为中性原子量子处理器实现任意深度量子电路奠定了坚实的基础。这种方法成功地解决了原子丢失带来的系统瓶颈，为未来实现纠错量子计算打下了重要基础。

Abstract: Neutral atom quantum processors are a promising platform for scalable quantum
computing. An obstacle to implementing deep quantum circuits is managing atom
loss, which constitutes a significant fraction of all errors. Current
approaches are either not capable of replacing lost atoms in the middle of a
circuit -- and therefore restricted to fixed, short circuit depths -- or
require more than an order of magnitude longer time than gate and measurement
operations to do so. In this work, we demonstrate fast, continuous atom
replacement leveraging the metastable $^{171}$Yb qubit. A continuously loaded
reservoir near the computation zone enables on-demand atom extraction with
tweezers up to 500 times per second. New qubit arrays can be prepared 30 times
per second when including single-atom preparation, non-destructive imaging and
initialization. Importantly, existing qubits are completely undisturbed by the
reloading process, owing to the extreme isolation of the metastable qubit from
cooling and imaging light. This work establishes a complete foundation for
implementing fast quantum circuits with unlimited depth, removing a final
roadblock for fault-tolerant quantum computing with neutral atoms.

TL;DR: This paper highlights the importance of exploiting error degeneracy to improve decoding performance in quantum error correction, achieving near-optimal frame error rates with high qubit counts.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the challenge of scalable quantum computation by improving error correction methods, aiming to achieve high-efficiency qubit codes.

Method: The authors devise an enhanced decoding algorithm that incorporates knowledge of error degeneracy to expedite the iterative decoding process, reducing the number of physical qubits needed and computational complexity.

Result: Simulations show a frame error rate of 1e-4 with 9.45% physical error rate, surpassing existing 1/3 rate codes, demonstrating significant progress towards quantum limits.

Conclusion: Exploiting quantum error degeneracy enhances decoding efficiency, proving vital for building large-scale quantum systems with qubit resource management.

Abstract: Quantum error correction is essential for realizing scalable quantum
computation. Among various approaches, low-density parity-check codes over
higher-order Galois fields have shown promising performance due to their
structured sparsity and compatibility with iterative decoding algorithms whose
computational complexity scales linearly with the number of physical qubits. In
this work, we demonstrate that explicitly exploiting the degeneracy of quantum
errors can significantly enhance the decoding performance. Simulation results
over the depolarizing channel indicate that the proposed method, at a coding
rate of 1/3, achieves a frame error rate as low as $10^{-4}$ at a physical
error rate of 9.45% for a code with 104,000 logical qubits and 312,000 physical
qubits, approaching the quantum hashing bound. These findings highlight the
critical role of degeneracy in closing the gap to the fundamental limits of
quantum error correction.

### [30] [Mitigating sloppiness in joint estimation of successive squeezing parameters](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15638)
*Priyanka Sharma,Stefano Olivares,Devendra Kumar Mishra,Matteo G. A. Paris*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: When two successive squeezing operations with the same phase are applied to a
field mode, reliably estimating the amplitude of each is impossible because the
output state depends solely on their sum. In this case, the quantum statistical
model becomes sloppy, and the quantum Fisher information matrix turns singular.
However, estimation of both parameters becomes feasible if the quantum state is
subjected to an appropriate scrambling operation between the two squeezing
operations. In this work, we analyze in detail the effects of a phase-shift
scrambling transformation, optimized to reduce sloppiness and maximize the
overall estimation precision. We also compare the optimized precision bounds of
joint estimation with those of stepwise estimation methods, finding that joint
estimation retains an advantage despite the quantum noise induced by the
residual parameter incompatibility. Finally, we analyze the precision
achievable by general-dyne detection and find that it may approach the optimal
precision in some regimes.

Abstract: Randomisation is widely used in quantum algorithms to reduce the number of
quantum gates and ancillary qubits required. A range of randomised algorithms,
including eigenstate property estimation by spectral filters, Hamiltonian
simulation, and perturbative quantum simulation, though motivated and designed
for different applications, share common features in the use of unitary
decomposition and Hadamard-test-based implementation. In this work, we start by
analysing the role of randomised linear-combination-of-unitaries (LCU) in
quantum simulations, and present several quantum circuits that realise the
randomised composite LCU. A caveat of randomisation, however, is that the
resulting state cannot be deterministically prepared, which often takes an
unphysical form $U \rho V^\dagger$ with unitaries $U$ and $V$. Therefore,
randomised LCU algorithms are typically restricted to only estimating the
expectation value of a single Pauli operator. To address this, we introduce a
quantum instrument that can realise a non-completely-positive map, whose
feature of frequent measurement and reset on the ancilla makes it particularly
suitable in the fault-tolerant regime. We then show how to construct an
unbiased estimator of the effective (unphysical) state $U \rho V^\dagger$ and
its generalisation. Moreover, we demonstrate how to effectively realise the
state prepared by applying an operator that admits a composite LCU form. Our
results reveal a natural connection between randomised LCU algorithms and
shadow tomography, thereby allowing simultaneous estimation of many observables
efficiently. As a concrete example, we construct the estimators and present the
simulation complexity for three use cases of randomised LCU in Hamiltonian
simulation and eigenstate preparation tasks.

### [32] [Wavefunction branches demand a definition!](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15663)
*C. Jess Riedel*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper evaluates different frameworks for defining quantum branches, focusing on quantum approachable sets and computational paths in Hilbert space, highlighting the potential for efficient classical simulation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: It addresses the unresolved issue of macroscopic quantum superpositions and their classical simulability, seeking formal methods to identify quantum branches beyond decoherence theory.

Method: Compares two existing approaches: quantum complexity and information-theoretic metrics, using analytic and numerical comparisons.

Result: Showcases potential and limitations of each framework, suggesting directions for further research in quantum branch definition and simulation.

Conclusion: Concludes that while both frameworks offer possibilities, further theoretical and computational work is needed to realize effective classical simulation of complex quantum systems.

Abstract: Under unitary evolution, a typical macroscopic quantum system is thought to
develop wavefunction branches: a time-dependent decomposition into orthogonal
components that (1) form a tree structure forward in time, (2) are approximate
eigenstates of quasiclassical macroscopic observables, and (3) exhibit
effective collapse of feasibly measurable observables. If they could be defined
precisely, wavefunction branches would extend the theory of decoherence beyond
the system-environment paradigm and could supplant anthropocentric measurement
in the quantum axioms. Furthermore, when such branches have bounded
entanglement and can be effectively identified numerically, sampling them would
allow asymptotically efficient classical simulation of quantum systems. I
consider a promising recent approach to formalizing branches on the lattice by
Taylor & McCulloch [Quantum 9, 1670 (2025), arXiv:2308.04494], and compare it
to prior work from Weingarten [Found. Phys. 52, 45 (2022), arXiv:2105.04545].
Both proposals are based on quantum complexity and argue that, once created,
branches persist for long times due to the generic linear growth of state
complexity. Taylor & McCulloch characterize branches by a large difference in
the unitary complexity necessary to interfere vs. distinguish them. Weingarten
takes branches as the components of the decomposition that minimizes a weighted
sum of expected squared complexity and the Shannon entropy of squared norms. I
discuss strengths and weaknesses of these approaches, and identify tractable
open questions.

</details>

Abstract: Eigenvalue estimation is a central problem for demonstrating quantum
advantage, yet its implementation on digital quantum computers remains limited
by circuit depth and operational overhead. We present an analog quantum phase
estimation (aQPE) protocol that extracts the eigenenergies of a target
Hamiltonian via continuous time evolution and single-mode cavity measurement.
By encoding eigenvalue information as conditional cavity phase-space rotations,
the scheme avoids deep quantum circuits and entangling gates, while enabling
readout through established cavity tomography techniques. We further illustrate
the feasibility of this approach by engineering a Hamiltonian that implements
aQPE of the XY model, whose ground-state energy problem is QMA-complete, within

experimental approaches have been proposed to probe quantum systems in curved

entanglement between quantum systems. Due to the symmetry of the configuration,
the proposed setup is insensitive to Newtonian gravitational contributions but
remains sensitive to the frame-dragging effect. Assuming the validity of the
quantum equivalence principle, this approach may provide insights not only into
the quantum nature of gravity but also into whether spacetime itself exhibits
quantum properties. However, our analysis reveals that, within realistic
experimental parameters, the expected effects are too small to be detected. We
discuss possible interpretations of this undetectability, and its implications
for tests of quantum gravity.

</details>


### [36] [The logical structure of contextuality and nonclassicality](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15071)

Paper proposes a mathematical framework using logic algebra to compare classical and quantum experiments, revealing that contextuality is a sufficient but not necessary condition for nonclassicality. They also demonstrate that nonclassicality can be present without contextuality. Additionally, the paper shows that using 12 projectors demonstrates the Kochen-Specker contextuality and that 3 measurements suffice to witness quantum contextuality, which is fewer than the 4 used in the compatibility graph approach.


<details>

Motivation: The paper addresses the relationship between contextuality and nonclassicality in quantum mechanics, aiming to provide a clearer understanding of these fundamental quantum phenomena and their interconnections.

Method: The authors develop a mathematical framework based on logic algebra to analyze and compare classical and quantum experiments. Experiments involving 12 projectors and 3 measurements are used to demonstrate their findings related to contextuality and nonclassicality.

Result: Contextuality is identified as a sufficient but not necessary condition for nonclassicality. Additionally, the paper shows that certain quantum experiments can exhibit nonclassicality without being contextual. The authors also demonstrate the efficiency of using fewer measurements (3) compared to the 4 used in another method (compatibility graph approach).

Conclusion: The paper concludes that quantum contextuality can be demonstrated with fewer resources than previously thought, and that nonclassicality can exist independently of contextuality, providing new insights into the nature of quantum mechanics.

Abstract: Quantum contextuality is known as the fundamental feature of quantum
mechanics. It is not clear whether contextuality fully reveals the nonclassical
aspects of quantum mechanics. To answer this question, we propose a
mathematical framework based on logic algebra to compare classical and quantum
experiments. With the framework, we precisely characterize the contextuality
and nonclassicality, reveal that the former is a sufficient but not necessary
condition for the latter, and present a type of quantum experiments which
exhibit nonclassicality without contextuality. We also point out that the
property of quantum systems is captured by the projector generators. Therefore,
it is possible to witness quantum contextuality with simplified measurement
configurations. For example, we show that 12 projectors witness the
Kochen-Specker contextuality, and 3 measurements are sufficient to witness the
quantum contextuality, as compared to the 4 presented in the compatibility
graph approach.

Abstract: We combine classical heuristics with partial shadow tomography to enable
efficient protocols for extracting information from correlated ab initio
electronic systems encoded on quantum devices. By proposing the use of a

in the energy estimate, as well as observing a linear scaling to accessible
system sizes. Furthermore, we find a high-degree of noise resilience of these

that these large system arguments do not prevent algorithmic advantage from

### [40] [Aperiodic Dissipation as a Mechanism for Steady-State Localization](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15108)
*Shilpi Roy,Jiangbin Gong*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: Dissipation is traditionally regarded as a disruptive factor in quantum
systems because it often leads to decoherence and delocalization. However,
recent insights into engineered dissipation reveal that it can be tuned to
facilitate various quantum effects, from state stabilization to phase
transitions. In this work, we identify aperiodic dissipation as a mechanism for
inducing steady-state localization, independent of disorder or a quasiperiodic
potential in the Hamiltonian. This localization arises from long-range phase
correlations introduced by a spatially varying dissipation phase parameter,
which enables nontrivial interference in the steady-state. By systematically
comparing two classes of aperiodic dissipation (defined as commensurate and
incommensurate cases), we find that incommensurate modulation plays the most
efficient role in stabilizing a localized steady-state. Our analysis, based on
coherence measures, purity, and participation ratio, reveals a direct link
between eigenstate coherence and real-space localization, showing that
dissipation can actively shape localization rather than simply causing
decoherence. These findings highlight aperiodic dissipation as a viable
approach to controlling localization in open quantum systems, potentially
enabling new ways to manipulate quantum states and design dissipation-driven
phases.

Abstract: Neutral-atom quantum computing (NAQC) offers distinct advantages such as
dynamic qubit reconfigurability, long coherence times, and high gate
fidelities, making it a promising platform for scalable quantum computing.

movements while preserving high circuit fidelity. Comparative evaluations
against state-of-the-art compilers demonstrate the superior performance of the
proposed methods. These methods could serve as benchmarks for evaluating the
performance of NAQC compilers.

Abstract: We show that the $T$-depth of any single-qubit $z$-rotation can be reduced to

Abstract: Whether gravity must be quantized remains one of the biggest open problems in
fundamental physics. Classical-quantum hybrid theories have recently attracted
attention as a possible framework in which gravity is treated classically yet
interacts consistently with quantum matter. Schemes based on completely

systematic treatment of quantum backreaction, but they also give rise to
features that challenge conventional physical intuition, such as the breakdown
of conservation laws. To illustrate this issue, we consider a qubit interacting

Abstract: Quantum multiparameter estimation aims to simultaneously estimate multiple
parameters from observing quantum systems and data processing. The complexity
of quantum multiparameter estimation arises primarily from measurement
incompatibility and parameter correlations. By manipulating the

tight for pure states and completely describes the quantum limit of
two-parameter estimation precision. We also develop an error ellipse method to

Method: The authors construct an analog of a traversable wormhole using the SYK model and TFD state framework. Abstract: This study aims to provide insights into various aspects of quantum chaos and
teleportation by implementing the recently developed Wormhole-Inspired
Teleportation Protocol (WITP). We commence by constructing an analog of a

with the Thermofield Double (TFD) state framework, implemented within a quantum

($\beta$) and the location of the message qubit, and compare the fidelity

SYK-based protocol achieves a higher fidelity of states in comparison to the
TFIM counterpart. We further analyze the protocol for different values of
$\beta$ and the SWAP operator. These findings are attributed to the emergence
of random matrix ensembles via random phase theory within the dynamics of the
SYK model, which is characterized by pronounced chaotic behavior. A significant
outcome of our investigation is initializing the message as a two-qubit Bell
state, followed by teleportation across the system. We introduce a Pauli
stabilizer-based fidelity measure to diagnose the teleportation
characteristics. This yields a considerable enhancement in fidelity relative to

fluctuation of fidelity for both single-qubit and two-qubit message across the
channel, contributing to a deeper understanding of quantum teleportation

Abstract: Equilibrium and nonequilibrium states of matter can exhibit fundamentally
different behavior. A key example is the Kardar-Parisi-Zhang universality class
in two spatial dimensions (2D KPZ), where microscopic deviations from
equilibrium give rise to macroscopic scaling laws without equilibrium
counterparts. While extensively studied theoretically, direct experimental
evidence of 2D KPZ scaling has remained limited to interface growth so far.
Here, we report the observation of universal scaling consistent with the KPZ
universality class in 2D exciton-polariton condensates -- quantum fluids of
light that are inherently driven and dissipative, thus breaking equilibrium
conditions. Using momentum-resolved photoluminescence spectroscopy as well as
space- and time-resolved interferometry, we probe the phase correlations across
microscopically different systems, varying drive conditions in two distinct
lattice geometries. Our analysis reveals correlation dynamics and scaling
exponents in excellent agreement with 2D KPZ predictions. These results
establish exciton-polariton condensates as a robust experimental platform for
exploring 2D nonequilibrium universality quantitatively, and open new avenues
for investigating the emergence of coherence in interacting quantum systems far
from equilibrium.

Abstract: Quantum neural networks (QNNs) are widely employed as ans\"atze for solving
variational problems, where their expressivity directly impacts performance.

impeding the optimal design of quantum circuits. In this work, we introduce the
effective rank, denoted as $\kappa$, as a novel quantitative measure of
expressivity. Specifically, $\kappa$ captures the number of effectively
independent parameters among all the variational parameters in a parameterized
quantum circuit, thus reflecting the true degrees of freedom contributing to

input data distributions, and measurement protocols, we demonstrate that

highly expressive quantum circuit configurations. To this end, we develop a
reinforcement learning framework featuring a self-attention transformer agent
that autonomously explores and optimizes circuit architectures. By integrating
theoretical characterization with practical optimization, our work establishes
$\kappa$ as a robust tool for quantifying QNN expressivity and demonstrates the
effectiveness of reinforcement learning in designing high-performance quantum
circuits. This study paves the way for building more expressive QNN

Abstract: Dynamical decoupling (DD) is a well-known open-loop protocol for suppressing
unwanted interactions in a quantum system, thereby drastically extending the
coherence time of useful quantum states. In the original framework of evolution
symmetrization, a DD sequence was shown to enforce a symmetry on the unwanted
Hamiltonian, thereby suppressing it if the symmetry was inaccessible. In this
work, we show how symmetries already present in the undesired Hamiltonian can
be harnessed to reduce the complexity of decoupling sequences and to construct
nested protocols that correct dominant errors at shorter timescales, using the
factorization of DD symmetry groups into a product of its subgroups. We provide
many relevant examples in various spin systems, using the Majorana
constellation and point-group factorization to identify and exploit symmetries
in the interaction Hamiltonian. Our framework recovers tailored pulse sequences
developed in the context of NMR and further produces novel short and robust
sequences capable of suppressing on-site disorder, dipole-dipole interactions,
and more exotic many-body interactions in spin ensembles.

information processing.

Abstract: Amplitude damping is a dominant source of error in high performance quantum
processors. A promising approach in quantum error correction is erasure error
conversion, where errors are converted into detectable leakage states.
Dual-rail encoding has been shown as a candidate for the conversion of
amplitude-damping errors; with unique sensitivities to noise and decoherence
sources. Here we present a dual-rail encoding within a single fixed-frequency
superconducting multimode transmon qubit. The three island, two junction device
comprises two transmonlike modes with a detuning of 0.75-1 GHz, in a coaxial
circuit QED architecture. We show the logical bit-flip and phase-flip error
rates are more than one order of magnitude lower than the physical error rates,
and demonstrate stability and repeatability of the architecture through an
extended measurement of three such devices. Finally, we discuss how the
error-detected subspace can be used for investigations into the fundamentals of
noise and decoherence in fixed-frequency transmon qubits.

Abstract: Randomized compilation protocols have recently attracted attention as
alternatives to traditional deterministic Trotter-Suzuki methods, potentially
reducing circuit depth and resource overhead. These protocols determine gate
application probabilities based on the strengths of Hamiltonian terms, as
measured by the trace norm. However, relying solely on the trace norm to define
sampling distributions may not be optimal, especially for continuous-variable
and hybrid-variable systems involving unbounded operators, where quantifying
Hamiltonian strengths is challenging. In this work, we propose an adaptive
randomized compilation algorithm that dynamically updates sampling weights via
low-order moment measurements of Hamiltonian terms, assigning higher
probabilities to terms with greater uncertainty. This approach improves
accuracy without significantly increasing gate counts and extends randomized
compilation to continuous-variable and hybrid-variable systems by addressing

terms. Numerical simulations demonstrate the effectiveness of our method.

Abstract: The universality of quantum theory has been questioned ever since it was
proposed. Key to this long-unsolved question is to test whether a given
physical system has non-classical features. Here we connect recently proposed

computer. Our result is robust, as it relies on minimal assumptions, and
remarkably it can be applied in a broad range of contexts, from quantum biology

Abstract: In this manuscript we discuss the relationship between the gate time of
Rydberg two-qubit gate and the Rydberg interaction strength. Different from the
two-qbuit gates that directly depend on the interactions between the spins (or
pseudo spins), the ones in atomic arrays are realized by driving the atoms to
the Rydberg states. As a consequence, competition happens between shortening
the gate time and decreasing the excitation probability of Rydberg states. For
the case of Rydberg blockade, it is found that the gate time is irrelevant of
the Rydberg interaction strength. In contrast, for the case of weak Rydberg
interactions, the interactions will help to accelerate the two-qubit gates.

the Rydberg blockade one to realize the two-qbuit gates under the same Rabi
frequencies of Rydberg excitation. Through using the geometric control under
the region of weak Rydberg interaction, fast and robust two-qubit gates can be
achieved in atomic arrays, of which detailed discussion can be referred to the
manuscript \textsl{arXiv:2412. 19193 (2024)}.

analytical threshold of the surface code under these types of correlated noise,
and find that errors correlated along straight lines possess a type of crucial
symmetry, resulting in higher thresholds compared to other types of correlated
errors. This deepens our insight into the threshold of surface code and hence
facilitates a more robust design of quantum circuits with a higher noise
threshold.

</details>


### [60] [${\sf QMA}={\sf QMA}_1$ with an infinite counter](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.15551)
*Stacey Jeffery,Freek Witteveen*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究显示QMA等于QMA^∞和QMA_1^∞，其中QMA_1^∞的验证者有一个无限大的寄存器，可以高效地进行移位操作。通过有限维构造，得出QMA增强器仅提高完备性，而降低时间为传统QMA增强器的对数时间。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究量子复杂性理论中的关键问题，是否有QMA等于QMA_1，试图通过引入无限寄存器的模型来探讨这个问题，可能与传统验证模型有本质区别。

Method: 研究通过构建无限寄存器模型来分析QMA的能力，利用概率 amplification和有限维构造技术来比较不同提升策略的优劣。

Result: 无限寄存器并不增强验证能力，而有限构造提升了许多效率。

Conclusion: QMA和它的无限增强版本并没有区别，但有限增强过程使得算法在时间上成本降低了很多。

Abstract: A long-standing open problem in quantum complexity theory is whether ${\sf
QMA}$, the quantum analogue of ${\sf NP}$, is equal to ${\sf QMA}_1$, its
one-sided error variant. We show that ${\sf QMA}={\sf QMA}^{\infty}= {\sf
QMA}_1^{\infty}$, where ${\sf QMA}_1^\infty$ is like ${\sf QMA}_1$, but the
verifier has an infinite register, as part of their witness system, in which
they can efficiently perform a shift (increment) operation. We call this
register an ``infinite counter'', and compare it to a program counter in a Las
Vegas algorithm. The result ${\sf QMA}={\sf QMA}^\infty$ means such an infinite
register does not increase the power of ${\sf QMA}$, but does imply perfect
completeness.
  By truncating our construction to finite dimensions, we get a ${\sf
QMA}$-amplifier that only amplifies completeness, not soundness, but does so in
significantly less time than previous ${\sf QMA}$ amplifiers. Our new
construction achieves completeness $1-2^{-q}$ using $O(1)$ calls to each of the
original verifier and its inverse, and $O(\log q)$ other gates, proving that
${\sf QMA}$ has completeness doubly exponentially close to 1, i.e. ${\sf
QMA}={\sf QMA}(1-2^{-2^r},2^{-r})$ for any polynomial $r$.

Method: 论文提出了一种连续的原子 reload 系统，利用$^{171}$Yb原子的长寿命特性。这个系统可以在0.02毫秒内完成一次 atom extraction，达到了每秒500次的频率。此外，通过同时进行单原子准备和非破坏性成像，可以在30次/秒的时间内准备新的 qubit arrays。系统的独特之处在于，通过孤立的原子特性，确保在 reload 过程中原有已被使用的原子不受影响。

Result: 通过这种方法，可以在计算中实现任意深度的量子电路，极大地扩展了量子计算的潜力。这篇论文消除了实现深度量子电路的最后障碍，为实现量子计算的大规模运算提供了可行的技术路径。这种方法不仅在理论上有突破，还在实际操作中非常高效，达到了很高的 reload 频率。

Conclusion: 这篇论文通过引入一种基于长寿命 $^{171}$Yb qubit 的原子 reload 体系，实现了量子处理器中快速替换丢失原子的问题。这种技术不仅在量子计算中具有重要意义，也为未来更长更深的量子电路提供了实现的可能性。这为量子计算的发展奠定了一个坚实的基础。

Abstract: Neutral atom quantum processors are a promising platform for scalable quantum
computing. An obstacle to implementing deep quantum circuits is managing atom
loss, which constitutes a significant fraction of all errors. Current
approaches are either not capable of replacing lost atoms in the middle of a
circuit -- and therefore restricted to fixed, short circuit depths -- or
require more than an order of magnitude longer time than gate and measurement
operations to do so. In this work, we demonstrate fast, continuous atom
replacement leveraging the metastable $^{171}$Yb qubit. A continuously loaded
reservoir near the computation zone enables on-demand atom extraction with
tweezers up to 500 times per second. New qubit arrays can be prepared 30 times
per second when including single-atom preparation, non-destructive imaging and
initialization. Importantly, existing qubits are completely undisturbed by the
reloading process, owing to the extreme isolation of the metastable qubit from
cooling and imaging light. This work establishes a complete foundation for

roadblock for fault-tolerant quantum computing with neutral atoms.

Abstract: When two successive squeezing operations with the same phase are applied to a
field mode, reliably estimating the amplitude of each is impossible because the
output state depends solely on their sum. In this case, the quantum statistical
model becomes sloppy, and the quantum Fisher information matrix turns singular.
However, estimation of both parameters becomes feasible if the quantum state is
subjected to an appropriate scrambling operation between the two squeezing
operations. In this work, we analyze in detail the effects of a phase-shift
scrambling transformation, optimized to reduce sloppiness and maximize the
overall estimation precision. We also compare the optimized precision bounds of
joint estimation with those of stepwise estimation methods, finding that joint
estimation retains an advantage despite the quantum noise induced by the
residual parameter incompatibility. Finally, we analyze the precision
achievable by general-dyne detection and find that it may approach the optimal
precision in some regimes.

Method: The paper presents a detailed analysis of randomised linear-combination-of-unitaries (LCU) within quantum simulations. Abstract: Randomisation is widely used in quantum algorithms to reduce the number of
quantum gates and ancillary qubits required. A range of randomised algorithms,
including eigenstate property estimation by spectral filters, Hamiltonian
simulation, and perturbative quantum simulation, though motivated and designed
for different applications, share common features in the use of unitary
decomposition and Hadamard-test-based implementation. In this work, we start by
analysing the role of randomised linear-combination-of-unitaries (LCU) in
quantum simulations, and present several quantum circuits that realise the
randomised composite LCU. A caveat of randomisation, however, is that the
resulting state cannot be deterministically prepared, which often takes an
unphysical form $U \rho V^\dagger$ with unitaries $U$ and $V$. Therefore,
randomised LCU algorithms are typically restricted to only estimating the
expectation value of a single Pauli operator. To address this, we introduce a
quantum instrument that can realise a non-completely-positive map, whose
feature of frequent measurement and reset on the ancilla makes it particularly
suitable in the fault-tolerant regime. We then show how to construct an
unbiased estimator of the effective (unphysical) state $U \rho V^\dagger$ and
its generalisation. Moreover, we demonstrate how to effectively realise the
state prepared by applying an operator that admits a composite LCU form. Our
results reveal a natural connection between randomised LCU algorithms and
shadow tomography, thereby allowing simultaneous estimation of many observables
efficiently. As a concrete example, we construct the estimators and present the
simulation complexity for three use cases of randomised LCU in Hamiltonian
simulation and eigenstate preparation tasks.

*C. Jess Riedel*

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: Under unitary evolution, a typical macroscopic quantum system is thought to
develop wavefunction branches: a time-dependent decomposition into orthogonal
components that (1) form a tree structure forward in time, (2) are approximate
eigenstates of quasiclassical macroscopic observables, and (3) exhibit
effective collapse of feasibly measurable observables. If they could be defined
precisely, wavefunction branches would extend the theory of decoherence beyond
the system-environment paradigm and could supplant anthropocentric measurement
in the quantum axioms. Furthermore, when such branches have bounded
entanglement and can be effectively identified numerically, sampling them would
allow asymptotically efficient classical simulation of quantum systems. I
consider a promising recent approach to formalizing branches on the lattice by
Taylor & McCulloch [Quantum 9, 1670 (2025), arXiv:2308.04494], and compare it
to prior work from Weingarten [Found. Phys. 52, 45 (2022), arXiv:2105.04545].
Both proposals are based on quantum complexity and argue that, once created,
branches persist for long times due to the generic linear growth of state
complexity. Taylor & McCulloch characterize branches by a large difference in
the unitary complexity necessary to interfere vs. distinguish them. Weingarten
takes branches as the components of the decomposition that minimizes a weighted
sum of expected squared complexity and the Shannon entropy of squared norms. I
discuss strengths and weaknesses of these approaches, and identify tractable
open questions.

</details>

The severe constraints of NISQ hardware, particularly in circuit depth and connectivity, hinder both the validation of quantum advantage and the empirical investigation of major obstacles like barren plateaus. Circuit cutting techniques have emerged as a strategy to execute larger quantum circuits on smaller, less connected hardware by dividing them into subcircuits. However, this partitioning increases the number of samples needed to estimate the expectation value accurately through classical post-processing compared to estimating it directly from the full circuit. This work introduces a novel regularization term into the QML optimization process, directly penalizing the overhead associated with sampling. We demonstrate that this approach enables the optimizer to balance the advantages of gate cutting against the optimization of the typical ML cost function. Specifically, it navigates the trade-off between minimizing the cutting overhead and maintaining the overall accuracy of the QML model, paving the way to study larger complex problems in pursuit of quantum advantage.

</details>

The lateral component of magnetic field of the magnetic dipole oscillating near a metallic surface is computed for the parameters of experiment in preparation which is aimed to directly check the validity of the Drude model in the area of transverse electric evanescent waves. By comparing with the case of graphene, whose dielectric response is spatially nonlocal and possesses the double pole at zero frequency, it is hypothesized that the success of the dissipationless plasma model in this area is also caused by the presence of a double pole.

### [73] [Long-Range Entangling Operations via Josephson Junction Metasurfaces](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14958)

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: 使用空间-时间调制的超导介lett面，通过工程化的波矢选择性耦合，替代了近场指数衰减的耦合方式，从而减小了量子比特之间的物理距离依赖性。利用iSWAP门和控制相位门，通过 resonate 和几何积聚的方法来实现双电容操作。

By modulating the surface in both space and time, we engineer sidebands with controllable wavevectors that selectively couple target qubits. The metasurface acts as a reconfigurable coupling medium, where the interaction strength is determined by engineered transmission coefficients rather than by exponentially decaying near-field coupling, thus reducing the dependence on physical proximity. We investigated the implementation of two-qubit interactions via iSWAP gates driven resonantly through the metasurface and controlled phase gates via geometric phase accumulation. We clarify the previous results for the objectivity study under what conditions the objectivity is achieved, especially how a trajectory of a central oscillator influences objectivity and why the objectivity is enhanced the phase get closer to $π/2$. We show that the finite number of environmental oscillators can have the objectivity only with respect to the associated time scales defined by frequency relation between a central oscillator and environmental oscillators. We study possible frequency relations for the objectivity and the associated time scales.
